href="/wiki/List_of_coastal_settlements_of_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of coastal settlements of the Mediterranean Sea">full list</a>)</i></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The&#160;<b>Mediterranean Sea</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">sea</a> connected to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> and almost completely enclosed by land: on the north by <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, on the south by <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> and on the east by the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. Although the sea is sometimes considered a part of the Atlantic Ocean, it is usually identified as a separate body of water. Geological evidence indicates that around 5.9 million years ago, the Mediterranean was cut off from the Atlantic and was partly or completely desiccated over a period of some 600,000 years, the <a href="/wiki/Messinian_salinity_crisis" title="Messinian salinity crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</a>, before being refilled by the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a> about 5.3 million years ago.\n</p><p>It covers an approximate area of 2.5 million km<sup>2</sup> (965,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), but its connection to the Atlantic (the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>) is only 14&#160;km (8.7&#160;mi) wide. The Strait of Gibraltar is a narrow strait that connects the Atlantic Ocean to the Mediterranean Sea and separates <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.  In <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a>, it is sometimes called the <i>Eurafrican Mediterranean Sea</i> or the <i>European Mediterranean Sea</i> to distinguish it from <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_sea_(oceanography)" title="Mediterranean sea (oceanography)">mediterranean seas</a> elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mediterranean Sea has an average depth of 1,500&#160;m (4,900&#160;ft) and  the deepest recorded point is 5,267&#160;m (17,280&#160;ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Calypso_Deep" title="Calypso Deep">Calypso Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a>. The sea is bordered on the north by <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, the east by <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, and in the south by <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.  It is located between latitudes <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_north" title="30th parallel north">30&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">46&#176; N</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">6&#176; W</a> and <a href="/wiki/36th_meridian_east" title="36th meridian east">36&#176; E</a>. Its west-east length, from the Strait of Gibraltar to the Gulf of Iskenderun, on the southwestern coast of Turkey, is approximately 4,000&#160;km (2,500 miles). The sea\'s average north-south length, from Croatia\'s southern shore to Libya, is approximately 800&#160;km (500 miles). The Mediterranean Sea, including the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> (connected by the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>), has a surface area of approximately 2,510,000 square km (970,000 square miles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sea was an important route for <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchants</a> and travellers of ancient times that allowed for trade and cultural exchange between emergent peoples of the region. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">history of the Mediterranean region</a> is crucial to understanding the origins and development of many modern societies.\n</p><p>The countries surrounding the Mediterranean in clockwise order are <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>; <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> are island countries in the sea. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">Akrotiri and Dhekelia</a> have coastlines on the sea.\n</p>\n<div biota</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Environmental_history"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Environmental history</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Natural_hazards"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Natural hazards</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Biodiversity"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Biodiversity</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28"><a href="#Invasive_species"><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Tourism"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Overfishing"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Overfishing</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_etymology">Names and etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names and etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/220px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/330px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/440px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>With its highly indented coastline and large number of islands, Greece has the longest Mediterranean coastline.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ancient Greeks called the Mediterranean simply <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#7969; &#952;&#940;&#955;&#945;&#963;&#963;&#945;</span> \'the Sea\' or sometimes <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#7969; &#956;&#949;&#947;&#940;&#955;&#8134; &#952;&#940;&#955;&#945;&#963;&#963;&#945;</span> \'the Great Sea\', <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#7969; &#7969;&#956;&#941;&#964;&#949;&#961;&#945; &#952;&#940;&#955;&#945;&#963;&#963;&#945;</span> \'Our Sea\', or <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#7969; &#952;&#940;&#955;&#945;&#963;&#963;&#945; &#7969; &#954;&#945;&#952;\'&#7969;&#956;&#8118;&#962;</span> \'the sea around us\'. The Romans called it <i>Mare Magnum</i> \'Great Sea\' or <i>Mare Internum</i> \'Internal Sea\' and, starting with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">Mare Nostrum</a></i> \'Our Sea\'. The term <i>Mare Mediterr&#257;neum</i> appears later: <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Julius_Solinus" title="Gaius Julius Solinus">Solinus</a> apparently used it in the 3rd century, but the earliest extant witness to it is in the 6th century, in <a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seirinidou_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-seirinidou-6">[6]</a></sup> It means \'in the middle of land, inland\' in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>, a compound of <i>medius</i> \'middle\', <i>terra</i> \'land, earth\' and <i>-&#257;neus</i> \'having the nature of\'. The Latin word is a <a href="/wiki/Calque" title="Calque">calque</a> of Greek <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#956;&#949;&#963;&#972;&#947;&#945;&#953;&#959;&#962;</span> \'inland\', from <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#956;&#941;&#963;&#959;&#962;</span> \'in the middle\' and <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#947;&#942;&#970;&#959;&#962;</span> \'of the earth\' (from <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">&#947;&#8134;</span> \'land, earth\'). The original meaning may have been \'the sea in the middle of the earth\', rather than \'the sea enclosed by land\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> called it the "Syrian Sea". In ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian" title="Syrian">Syrian</a> texts, <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician</a> epics and in the Hebrew <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a>, it was primarily known as the "Great Sea" (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r867359662">.mw-parser-output .script-hebrew,.mw-parser-output .script-Hebr{font-size:1.15em;font-family:"Ezra SIL","Ezra SIL SR","Keter Aram Tsova","Taamey Ashkenaz","Taamey David CLM","Taamey Frank CLM","Frank Ruehl CLM","Keter YG","Shofar","David CLM","Hadasim CLM","Simple CLM","Nachlieli","SBL BibLit","SBL Hebrew",Cardo,Alef,"Noto Serif Hebrew","Noto Sans Hebrew","David Libre",David,"Times New Roman",Gisha,Arial,FreeSerif,FreeSans}</style><span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%;">&#1492;&#1463;&#1497;&#1464;&#1468;&#1501; &#1492;&#1463;&#1490;&#1464;&#1468;&#1491;&#1493;&#1465;&#1500;</span>&#8236;, <i>HaYam HaGadol</i>, <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Numbers" title="Book of Numbers">Numbers</a> 34:6,7; <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Joshua" title="Book of Joshua">Joshua</a> 1:4, 9:1, 15:47; <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">Ezekiel</a> 47:10,15,20) or simply as "The Sea" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Kings" title="1 Kings">1 Kings</a> 5:9; <i>compare</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Macc." title="1 Macc.">1 Macc.</a> 14:34, 15:11); however, it has also been called the "Hinder Sea" (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r867359662" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%;">&#1492;&#1463;&#1497;&#1464;&#1468;&#1501; &#1492;&#1464;&#1488;&#1463;&#1495;&#1458;&#1512;&#1493;&#1465;&#1503;</span>&#8236;) because of its location on the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" title="Greater Syria">Greater Syria</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> (and therefore behind a person facing the east), which is sometimes translated as "Western Sea", (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deuteronomy" title="Deuteronomy">Deut.</a> 11:24; <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Joel" title="Book of Joel">Joel</a> 2:20). Another name was the "Sea of the <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">Philistines</a>" (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r867359662" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%;">&#1497;&#1464;&#1501; &#1508;&#1456;&#1468;&#1500;&#1460;&#1513;&#1456;&#1473;&#1514;&#1460;&#1468;&#1497;&#1501;</span>&#8236;, <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" title="Book of Exodus">Exod.</a> 23:31), from the people inhabiting a large portion of its shores near the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Modern_Hebrew" title="Modern Hebrew">Modern Hebrew</a>, it is called <i>HaYam HaTikhon</i> (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r867359662" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%;">&#1492;&#1463;&#1497;&#1464;&#1468;&#1501; &#1492;&#1463;&#1514;&#1460;&#1468;&#1497;&#1499;&#1493;&#1465;&#1503;</span>&#8236;) \'the Middle Sea\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-melitensia-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Arabic</a>, it is known as <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="American Library Association &#8211; Library of Congress transliteration">al-Ba&#7717;r [al-Abya&#7693;] al-Mutawassi&#7789;</i></i> (<span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1575;&#1604;&#1576;&#1581;&#1585; [&#1575;&#1604;&#1571;&#1576;&#1610;&#1590;] &#1575;&#1604;&#1605;&#1578;&#1608;&#1587;&#1591;</span>) \'the [White] Middle Sea\'. In Islamic and older Arabic literature, it was <i>Ba&#7717;r al-R&#363;m(&#299;)</i> (<span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1576;&#1581;&#1585; &#1575;&#1604;&#1585;&#1608;&#1605;</span> or <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1576;&#1581;&#1585; &#1575;&#1604;&#1585;&#1608;&#1605;&#1610;</span>}) \'the Sea of the Romans\' or \'the Roman Sea\'. At first, that name referred to only the Eastern Mediterranean, but it was later extended to the whole Mediterranean. Other Arabic names were <i>Ba&#7717;r al-&#353;&#257;m(&#299;)</i> (<span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1576;&#1581;&#1585; &#1575;&#1604;&#1588;&#1575;&#1605;</span>) \'the Sea of Syria\' and <i>Ba&#7717;r al-Maghrib</i> (<span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1576;&#1581;&#1585;&#1575;&#1604;&#1605;&#1594;&#1585;&#1576;</span>) \'the Sea of the West\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoi_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-eoi-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seirinidou_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-seirinidou-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, it is the <i>Akdeniz</i> \'the White Sea\'; in Ottoman, &#65153;&#1602; &#1583;&#1603;&#1610;&#1586;, which sometimes means only the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The origin of the name is not clear, as it is not known in earlier Greek, Byzantine or Islamic sources. It may be to contrast with the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoi_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-eoi-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-melitensia-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In Persian, the name was translated as <i>Ba&#7717;r-i Saf&#299;d</i>, which was also used in later <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a>. It is probably the origin of the colloquial Greek &#902;&#963;&#960;&#961;&#951; &#920;&#940;&#955;&#945;&#963;&#963;&#945;.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eoi_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-eoi-10">[10]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Johann_Knobloch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Johann Knobloch (page does not exist)">Johann Knobloch</a> claims that in Classical Antiquity, cultures in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> used colours to refer to the cardinal points: black referred to the north (explaining the name <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>), yellow or blue to east, red to south (i.e., the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>), and <i>white</i> to west. This would explain both the Turkish <i>Akdeniz</i> (White Sea) and the Arab nomenclature described above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">History of the Mediterranean region</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_civilizations">Ancient civilizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient civilizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1616" data-file-width="2836" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/220px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/330px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/440px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greek (red) and Phoenician (yellow) <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">colonies in antiquity</a> c. the 6th century BCE</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="2534" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/220px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/330px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/440px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> at its farthest extent in AD 117</div></div></div>\n<p>Several ancient civilizations were located around the Mediterranean shores and were greatly influenced by their proximity to the sea. It provided routes for trade, colonization, and war, as well as food (from fishing and the gathering of other seafood) for numerous communities throughout the ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the shared climate, geology, and access to the sea, cultures centered on the Mediterranean tended to have some extent of intertwined culture and history.\n</p><p>Two of the most notable Mediterranean civilizations in <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> were the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_state" title="City state">city states</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, both of which extensively colonized the coastlines of the Mediterranean. Later, when <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, the Romans referred to the Mediterranean as <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">Mare Nostrum</a></i> ("Our Sea"). For the next 400 years, the Roman Empire completely controlled the Mediterranean Sea and virtually all its coastal regions from Gibraltar to the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darius_I_of_Persia" title="Darius I of Persia">Darius I of Persia</a>, who conquered <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egypt</a>, built a canal linking the Mediterranean to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>. Darius\'s canal was wide enough for two <a href="/wiki/Trireme" title="Trireme">triremes</a> to pass each other with oars extended, and required four days to traverse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_empires">Middle Ages and empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1341" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a>, 1571, ended in victory for the European <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">Holy League</a> against the Ottoman Turks.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> collapsed around AD 476. Temporarily the east was again dominant as Roman power lived on in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> formed in the 4th century from the eastern half of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. Another power arose in the 7th century, and with it the religion of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, which soon swept across from the east; at its greatest extent, the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Arab Empire</a> controlled 75% of the Mediterranean region and left a lasting footprint on its eastern and southern shores.\n</p><p>The Arab invasions disrupted the trade relations between Western and Eastern Europe while cutting the trade route with Oriental lands. This, however, had the indirect effect of promoting the trade across the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>. The export of grains from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> was re-routed towards the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern world</a>. Oriental goods like silk and spices were carried from Egypt to ports like <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> by sailors and Jewish merchants. The <a href="/wiki/Viking_expansion" title="Viking expansion">Viking raids</a> further disrupted the trade in western Europe and brought it to a halt. However, the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norsemen</a> developed the trade from Norway to the <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Sea</a>, while also trading in luxury goods from <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Spain</a> and the Mediterranean. The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire_under_the_Isaurian_dynasty" title="Byzantine Empire under the Isaurian dynasty">Byzantines in the mid-8th century</a> retook control of the area around the north-eastern part of the Mediterranean. Venetian ships from the 9th century armed themselves to counter the harassment by Arabs while concentrating trade of oriental goods at Venice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatimids" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a> maintained trade relations with the <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">Italian city-states</a> like <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Amalfi" title="Duchy of Amalfi">Amalfi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoa</a>  before the Crusades, according to the <a href="/wiki/Cairo_Geniza" title="Cairo Geniza">Cairo Geniza</a> documents. A document dated 996 mentions Amalfian merchants living in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. Another letter states that the Genoese had traded with <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>. The caliph <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ma%27ad_al-Mustansir_Billah" title="Ma\'ad al-Mustansir Billah">al-Mustansir</a> had allowed Amalfian merchants to reside in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> about 1060 in place of the Latin <a href="/wiki/Hospice" title="Hospice">hospice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> led to flourishing of trade between Europe and the <i><a href="/wiki/Outremer" title="Outremer">outremer</a></i> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Genoa, Venica and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Pisa" title="Republic of Pisa">Pisa</a> created colonies in regions controlled by the Crusaders and came to control the trade with the Orient. These colonies also allowed them to trade with the Eastern world. Though the fall of the Crusader states and attempts at banning of trade relations with Muslim states by the Popes temporarily disrupted the trade with the Orient, it however continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Europe started to revive, however, as more organized and centralized states began to form in the later <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_of_the_12th_century" title="Renaissance of the 12th century">Renaissance of the 12th century</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2061" data-file-width="2940" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/220px-thumbnail.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/330px-thumbnail.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/440px-thumbnail.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">bombardment of Algiers</a> by the Anglo-Dutch fleet in support of an ultimatum to release European slaves, August 1816</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> power based in Anatolia continued to grow, and in 1453 extinguished the Byzantine Empire with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Constantinople" title="Conquest of Constantinople">Conquest of Constantinople</a>. Ottomans gained control of much of the sea in the 16th century and maintained naval bases in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_occupation_of_Toulon" title="Ottoman occupation of Toulon">southern France</a> (1543-1544), Algeria and Tunisia. <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Barbarossa</a>, the famous Ottoman captain is a symbol of this domination with the victory of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza" title="Battle of Preveza">Battle of Preveza</a> (1538). The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Djerba" title="Battle of Djerba">Battle of Djerba</a> (1560) marked the apex of Ottoman naval domination in the Mediterranean. As the naval prowess of the European powers increased, they confronted Ottoman expansion in the region when the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> (1571) checked the power of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Ottoman Navy</a>. This was the last naval battle to be fought primarily between <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">galleys</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Africa" title="Northwest Africa">Northwest Africa</a> preyed on Christian shipping and coastlines in the Western Mediterranean Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> According to Robert Davis, from the 16th to 19th centuries, pirates captured 1 million to 1.25 million Europeans as slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The development of oceanic shipping began to affect the entire Mediterranean. Once, most trade between Western Europe and the East had passed through the region, but after the 1490s the development of a sea route to the Indian Ocean allowed the importation of Asian <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spices</a> and other goods through the Atlantic ports of western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sea remained strategically important. British mastery of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> ensured their influence in Africa and Southwest Asia. Wars included <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare_in_the_Mediterranean_during_World_War_I" title="Naval warfare in the Mediterranean during World War I">Naval warfare in the Mediterranean during World War I</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century_and_migrations">21st century and migrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century and migrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width: 272px;">\n<div class="thumbimage" style="width: 270px; height: 110px; overflow: hidden;">\n<div style="position: relative; top: -265px; left: -1055px; width: 2200px"><div class="noresize"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="21600" data-file-width="43200" decoding="async" height="1100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/2200px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/3300px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/4400px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 2x" width="2200"/></a></div></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg" title="File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">Satellite image</a> of the Mediterranean Sea at night\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 2013 the Maltese president described the Mediterranean sea as a "cemetery" due to the large number of migrants who drowned there after their boats capsized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> European Parliament president <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">Martin Schulz</a> said in 2014 that Europe\'s migration policy "turned the Mediterranean into a graveyard", referring to the number of drowned refugees in the region as a direct result of the policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> An Azerbaijani official described the sea as "a burial ground ... where people die".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2013_Lampedusa_migrant_shipwreck" title="2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck">2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">Italian government</a> decided to strengthen the national system for the patrolling of the Mediterranean Sea by authorising "<a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Operation Mare Nostrum</a>", a military and humanitarian mission in order to rescue the migrants and arrest the traffickers of immigrants. In 2015, more than one million migrants crossed the Mediterranean Sea into Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Italy was particularly affected by the <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">European migrant crisis</a>. Since 2013, over 700,000 migrants have landed in Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> mainly sub-Saharan Africans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5222" data-file-width="5275" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/180px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/270px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/360px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A satellite image showing the Mediterranean Sea. The <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> can be seen in the bottom left (north-west) quarter of the image; to its left is the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and to its right, the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="653" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/180px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/270px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/360px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Straits" title="Turkish Straits">strait</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. The north side is <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelibolu_Peninsula" title="Gelibolu Peninsula">Gelibolu Peninsula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> region; the south side is <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The Mediterranean Sea is connected to the Atlantic Ocean by the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> (known in <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a>\'s writings as the "<a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">Pillars of Hercules</a>") in the west and to the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">Sea of Marmara</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">Bosporus</a> respectively, in the east. The Sea of Marmara (<a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a>) is often considered a part of the Mediterranean Sea, whereas the Black Sea is generally not. The 163&#160;km (101&#160;mi) long artificial <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in the southeast connects the Mediterranean Sea to the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-melitensia-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Large islands in the Mediterranean include <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euboea" title="Euboea">Euboea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesbos_Island" title="Lesbos Island">Lesbos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kefalonia" title="Kefalonia">Kefalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limnos" title="Limnos">Limnos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samos" title="Samos">Samos</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naxos_Island" title="Naxos Island">Naxos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andros" title="Andros">Andros</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cres" title="Cres">Cres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krk" title="Krk">Krk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bra%C4%8D" title="Bra&#269;">Bra&#269;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hvar" title="Hvar">Hvar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pag_(island)" title="Pag (island)">Pag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kor%C4%8Dula" title="Kor&#269;ula">Kor&#269;ula</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malta_Island" title="Malta Island">Malta</a> in the central Mediterranean; <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">Ibiza</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>  in the Western Mediterranean.\n</p><p>The typical <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> has hot, humid, and dry summers and mild, rainy winters. Crops of the region include <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">tangerines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">cork</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">Extent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Extent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> defines the limits of the Mediterranean Sea as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-IHO-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> in the west to the entrances to the <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">Dardanelles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> in the east, the Mediterranean Sea is bounded by the coasts of Europe, Africa and Asia, and is divided into two deep basins:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Western Basin:\n<ul><li>On the west: A line joining the extremities of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Trafalgar" title="Cape Trafalgar">Cape Trafalgar</a> (Spain) and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Spartel" title="Cape Spartel">Cape Spartel</a> (Africa).</li>\n<li>On the northeast: The west coast of Italy. In the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina" title="Strait of Messina">Strait of Messina</a> a line joining the north extreme of Cape Paci (15&#176;42\'E) with Cape Peloro, the east extreme of the Island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>. The north coast of Sicily.</li>\n<li>On the east: A line joining Cape Lilibeo the western point of Sicily (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;params=37_47_N_12_22_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">37&#176;47&#8242;N</span> <span class="longitude">12&#176;22&#8242;E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">37.783&#176;N 12.367&#176;E</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">37.783; 12.367</span></span></span></a></span>), through the Adventure Bank to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bon" title="Cape Bon">Cape Bon</a> (Tunisia).</li></ul></li>\n<li>Eastern Basin:\n<ul><li>On the west: The northeastern and eastern limits of the Western Basin.</li>\n<li>On the northeast: A line joining <a href="/wiki/Kumkale,_%C3%87anakkale" title="Kumkale, &#199;anakkale">Kum Kale</a> (26&#176;11\'E) and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Helles" title="Cape Helles">Cape Helles</a>, the western entrance to the Dardanelles.</li>\n<li>On the southeast: The entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>.</li>\n<li>On the east: The coasts of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offshore_Oil_Fields">Offshore Oil Fields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Offshore Oil Fields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Oil-drilling platforms and submarine pipelines are operational in several areas of the Mediterranean, including the coast of <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Palestine" title="Palestine">Palestine</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceanography">Oceanography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Oceanography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="497" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF/360px-MEDCURR.GIF" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF 1.5x" width="360"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Predominant surface currents for June</div></div></div>\n<p>Being nearly landlocked affects conditions in the Mediterranean Sea: for instance, <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tides</a> are very limited as a result of the narrow connection with the Atlantic Ocean. The Mediterranean is characterised and immediately recognised by its deep blue colour.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">Evaporation</a> greatly exceeds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> and river runoff in the Mediterranean, a fact that is central to the water circulation within the basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Evaporation is especially high in its eastern half, causing the water level to decrease and <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">salinity</a> to increase eastward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The salinity at 5 m depth is 3.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pressure_gradient" title="Pressure gradient">pressure gradient</a> pushes relatively cool, low-salinity water from the Atlantic across the basin; it warms and becomes saltier as it travels east, then sinks in the region of the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> and circulates westward, to spill over the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Thus, seawater flow is eastward in the Strait\'s surface waters, and westward below; once in the Atlantic, this chemically distinct Mediterranean Intermediate Water can persist thousands of kilometres away from its source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The temperature of the water in the deepest part of the Mediterranean Sea is 13.2&#160;&#176;C (55.8&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_countries">Coastal countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Coastal countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mediterranean_countries" title="List of Mediterranean countries">List of Mediterranean countries</a>.</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Relief,_1028_x_1024.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1828" decoding="async" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg/360px-Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg/540px-Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg/720px-Mediterranean_Relief%2C_1028_x_1024.jpg 2x" width="360"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Relief,_1028_x_1024.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Mediterranean Sea</div></div></div>\n<p>The following countries have a coastline on the Mediterranean Sea:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Northern shore</b> (from west to east): <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Eastern shore</b> (from north to south): <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Southern shore</b> (from west to east): <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Island nations</b>: <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Several other territories also border the Mediterranean Sea (from west to east): The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, the Spanish autonomous cities of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberan&#237;a">nearby islands</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas" title="Sovereign Base Areas">Sovereign Base Areas</a> on Cyprus, and the Palestinian <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" title="Latakia">Latakia</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Tunisia\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Sfax" title="Sfax">Sfax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sousse" title="Sousse">Sousse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Turkey\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Adana" title="Adana">Adana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antalya" title="Antalya">Antalya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> (through the Sea of Marmara), <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="&#304;zmir">&#304;zmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mersin" title="Mersin">Mersin</a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="811" data-file-width="1208" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Africa (left, on horizon) and Europe (right), as seen from Gibraltar</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> (IHO) divides the Mediterranean into a number of smaller waterbodies, each with their own designation (from west to east):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-IHO-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Sea" title="Alboran Sea">Alboran Sea</a>, between Spain and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">Balearic Sea</a>, between mainland Spain and its <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_Sea" title="Ligurian Sea">Ligurian Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a> (Italy);</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">Tyrrhenian Sea</a> enclosed by <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_peninsula" title="Italian peninsula">Italian peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a> between Italy, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and Greece;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a> between Italy, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a> between Greece and Turkey.</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_seas">Other seas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other seas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2591" data-file-width="3870" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/220px-Positano_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/330px-Positano_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/440px-Positano_-_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Positano" title="Positano">Positano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">Tyrrhenian Sea</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Some other seas whose names have been in common use from the ancient times, or in the present:\n</p>\n<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sardinia" title="Sea of Sardinia">Sea of Sardinia</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">Balearic Sea</a></li>\n<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sicily" title="Sea of Sicily">Sea of Sicily</a> between <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>,</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Sea" title="Libyan Sea">Libyan Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>,</li>\n<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>,\n<ul><li>the <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Sea" title="Thracian Sea">Thracian Sea</a> in its north,</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Myrtoan_Sea" title="Myrtoan Sea">Myrtoan Sea</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cyclades</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a>,</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Crete" title="Sea of Crete">Sea of Crete</a> north of Crete,</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Icarian_Sea" title="Icarian Sea">Icarian Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a></li></ul></li>\n<li>the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilician_Sea" title="Cilician Sea">Cilician Sea</a> between Turkey and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a></li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Sea" title="Levantine Sea">Levantine Sea</a> at the eastern end of the Mediterranean</li></ul>\n<p>Many of these smaller seas feature in local myth and folklore and derive their names from these associations.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_features">Other features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a south of France</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Valencia" title="Gulf of Valencia">Gulf of Valencia</a>, east of Spain</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina" title="Strait of class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:auto; max-width:777px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the K&#246;ppen climate classification"><img alt="" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="769" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Koppen_World_Map_%28Mediterranean_Sea_area_only%29.png" width="769"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="File:Koppen World Map (Mediterranean Sea area only).png"> </a></div>Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate classification</a></div>\n</div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea_temperature">Sea temperature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="wikitable">\n<caption>Mean sea temperature (&#176;C)\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>Jan\n</th>\n<th>Feb\n</th>\n<th>Mar\n</th>\n<th>Apr\n</th>\n<th>May\n</th>\n<th>Jun\n</th>\n<th>Jul\n</th>\n<th>Aug\n</th>\n<th>Sep\n</th>\n<th>Oct\n</th>\n<th>Nov\n</th>\n<th>Dec\n</th>\n<th>Year\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>18\n</td>\n<td>17\n</td>\n<td>17\n</td>\n<td>18\n</td>\n<td>21\n</td>\n<td>24\n</td>\n<td>26\n</td>\n<td>28\n</td>\n<td>27\n</td>\n<td>26\n</td>\n<td>23\n</td>\n<td>20\n</td>\n<th>22.1\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geology_and_paleoclimatology_of_the_Mediterranean_Basin" title="Geology and paleoclimatology of the Mediterranean Basin">Geology and paleoclimatology of the Mediterranean Basin</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/220px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/330px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg/440px-Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vrulja_kod_Omi%C5%A1a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A submarine <a href="/wiki/Karst_spring" title="Karst spring">karst spring</a>, called <i>vrulja</i>, near <a href="/wiki/Omi%C5%A1" title="Omi&#353;">Omi&#353;</a>; observed through several ripplings of an otherwise calm sea surface.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geologic history</a> of the Mediterranean Sea is complex. Underlain by <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a>, the sea basin was once thought to be a tectonic remnant of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">Tethys Ocean</a>; it is now known to be a structurally younger basin, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotethys" title="Neotethys">Neotethys</a>, which was first formed by the convergence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_plate" title="African plate">African</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_plate" title="Eurasian plate">Eurasian plates</a> during the Late <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> and Early <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a>. Because it is a near-landlocked body of water in a normally dry climate, the Mediterranean is subject to intensive evaporation and the precipitation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evaporites" title="Evaporites">evaporites</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Messinian_salinity_crisis" title="Messinian salinity crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</a> started about six million years ago (mya) when the Mediterranean became landlocked, and then essentially dried up. There are salt deposits accumulated on the bottom of the basin of more than a million cubic kilometres&#8212;in some places more than three kilometres thick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scientists estimate that the sea was last filled about 5.3 million years ago (mya)  in less than two years by the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a>.  Water poured in from the Atlantic Ocean through a newly breached gateway now called the   <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> at an estimated rate of about three orders of magnitude (one thousand times) larger than the current flow of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCetal2009_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-GCetal2009-54">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mediterranean Sea has an average depth of 1,500&#160;m (4,900&#160;ft) and the deepest recorded point is 5,267&#160;m (17,280&#160;ft) in the <a href="/wiki/Calypso_Deep" title="Calypso Deep">Calypso Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a>. The coastline extends for 46,000&#160;km (29,000&#160;mi). A shallow submarine ridge (the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Sicily" title="Strait of Sicily">Strait of Sicily</a>) between the island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and the coast of <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> divides the sea in two main subregions: the Western Mediterranean, with an area of about 850 thousand&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (330 thousand&#160;mi<sup>2</sup>); and the Eastern Mediterranean, of about 1.65 million&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (640 thousand&#160;mi<sup>2</sup>). A characteristic of the coastal Mediterranean are submarine <a href="/wiki/Karst_spring" title="Karst spring">karst springs</a> or <i lang="hr" title="Croatian language text">vrulja</i>s, which discharge pressurised groundwater into the coastal seawater from below the surface; the discharge water is usually fresh,  and sometimes may be thermal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaMoreaux2001_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaMoreaux2001-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tectonics_and_paleoenvironmental_analysis">Tectonics and paleoenvironmental analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tectonics and paleoenvironmental analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Mediterranean basin and sea system was established by the ancient African-Arabian continent colliding with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian" title="Eurasian">Eurasian</a> continent. As Africa-Arabia drifted northward, it closed over the ancient <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">Tethys Ocean</a> which had earlier separated the two supercontinents <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a>.\nAt about that time in the middle <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> period (roughly 170 million years ago<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2018)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Mediterranean_Sea#Dubious" title="Talk:Mediterranean Sea">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>) a much smaller sea basin, dubbed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotethys" title="Neotethys">Neotethys</a>, was formed shortly before the Tethys Ocean closed at its western (Arabian) end. The broad line of collisions pushed up a very long system of mountains from the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> in Spain to the <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros Mountains</a> in Iran in an episode of mountain-building tectonics known as the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_orogeny" title="Alpine orogeny">Alpine orogeny</a>. The Neotethys grew larger during the episodes of collisions (and associated foldings and subductions) that occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> epochs (34 to 5.33 mya); <i>see</i> animation: <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">Africa-Arabia colliding with Eurasia</a>. Accordingly, the Mediterranean <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_basin" title="Oceanic basin">basin</a> consists of several stretched <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonic</a> plates in subduction which are the foundation of the Eastern part of the Mediterranean Sea. Various zones of subduction harbour and form the <a href="/wiki/Deep_sea" title="Deep sea">deepest</a> and most majestic oceanic ridges, east of the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">Ionian Sea</a> and south of the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Indian_Ridge" title="Central Indian Ridge">Central Indian Ridge</a> runs East of the Mediterranean Sea South-East across the in-between of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Messinian_salinity_crisis">Messinian salinity crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Messinian salinity crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Etapa3muda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Messinian salinity crisis before the <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">Zanclean flood</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform"
